# PLAN: Full-Stack Audit + Dutchie Sync Hardening + Universal Theme System

## Verified API facts (Sol: trust these over Swagger)

- Auth: `Authorization: Basic base64(apiKey + ':')`
- Transactions: `GET /reporting/transactions` — `FromDateUTC`/`ToDateUTC` (max 60-day window; chunk at 55), `IncludeDetail=true`, `IncludeTaxes=true`
- Customers: `GET /customer/customers-paginated` — `PageNumber`/`PageSize` (max 1000), supports `fromLastModifiedDateUTC`
- Products: `GET /products` — single request returns all; supports `fromLastModifiedDateUTC`
- Inventory: `GET /reporting/inventory` — `Skip`/`Take` (max 5000) (`/inventory` returns empty — do not use)
- Employees: `GET /employees` — fields are `userId`, `fullName`, `status`, `groups`
- Loyalty: `GET /reporting/loyalty-snapshot` — no params, returns ALL customers `[{customerId:int, loyaltyBalance:double, loyaltySpent:double, loyaltyEarned:double}]`, rate-limited 1/min, nightly-refreshed
- Supabase gotchas: 1000-row default limit (page with `.range()` in 1000 chunks); PostgREST upsert needs a real UNIQUE constraint; dedupe batch upserts by conflict key; `NOTIFY pgrst, 'reload schema'` after DDL.
- MANDATORY: read `DATABASE-CONSTRAINTS.md` before any insert/update code. Only CHECK-listed enum values.

## Phase A — Site-wide audit & fix (broken links, APIs, schemas, UI, edge cases)

Scale: 102 pages, 229 API routes, 84 components.

Method (Sol executes in this order, recording every finding in `.route/AUDIT.md` as `A-<n>: <file:line> — <problem> — <fix>`):

1. **Route inventory**: enumerate all `page.tsx` paths → the set of real routes. Grep all `href=`, `router.push(`, `redirect(` targets in `src/` → flag + fix any target not in the set (or dynamic targets whose base segment doesn't exist).
2. **API call inventory**: grep all `fetch('/api/...')` client calls → verify each path has a matching `route.ts` exporting that HTTP method. Flag + fix mismatches, including response-shape mismatches (known bug class: pages reading `json.data` when routes return named keys).
3. **Schema conformance**: cross-check every `.insert(`/`.update(`/`.upsert(` payload against `DATABASE-CONSTRAINTS.md` CHECK constraints and NOT NULLs. Fix any value not in the allowed list. Known bug classes: invented enum values, missing org/location scoping.
4. **UI dead-ends**: buttons with no-op/missing handlers, forms whose submit hits a nonexistent endpoint, modals that can't close, `onClick` referencing undefined functions, HTML entity corruption (`&apos;` rendered literally), dropdowns clipped by `overflow-hidden` parents.
5. **Edge cases**: null `locationId` (all-locations mode) crashes, empty-array `.map` states with no empty-state UI on list pages, unguarded `.toFixed()`/date parses on nullable fields, division by zero in stats.
6. **Known open bug**: Dutchie settings page Sync History table shows `--` in DATE column — the log API/response field mapping is broken; fix so real timestamps render (US Mountain time).

Acceptance criteria:
- AC-A1: `.route/AUDIT.md` lists every finding with file:line and the applied fix; zero findings left in "found but unfixed" state (or explicitly justified as out-of-scope with reason).
- AC-A2: Every internal `href`/`router.push` target resolves to an existing route (verified by the inventory script output included in AUDIT.md).
- AC-A3: Every client `fetch('/api/…')` has a matching route handler + method, and the consuming code reads the actual response keys.
- AC-A4: No DB write path uses enum values absent from DATABASE-CONSTRAINTS.md.
- AC-A5: Sync History DATE column renders real dates.
- AC-A6: No page crashes on null location selection (spot-fix any found).

## Phase B — Dutchie sync: hardening + loyalty points sync

B1. **Loyalty sync (new entity)** — schema facts VERIFIED on dev 2026-07-14:
- `loyalty_balances` columns: `current_points` INTEGER NOT NULL, `lifetime_points` INTEGER NOT NULL, `customer_id` UUID NOT NULL, `organization_id` UUID NOT NULL, `enrolled_at` TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL, `tier_id` nullable. UNIQUE `(customer_id, organization_id)` exists (upsert conflict key ready). `customers.dutchie_customer_id` INTEGER exists.
- Migration `2026xxxx_dutchie_loyalty_sync.sql`: (1) widen `loyalty_balances.current_points` and `lifetime_points` to `NUMERIC(12,2)` — Dutchie balances are decimals (live sample: 162.27) and INTEGER would silently truncate customer points; (2) add `sync_loyalty BOOLEAN DEFAULT TRUE` and `last_synced_loyalty_at TIMESTAMPTZ` to `dutchie_config`; (3) `NOTIFY pgrst, 'reload schema'`. Audit any code doing integer math on these columns.
- `syncEngine.ts`: new `syncLoyalty` — one snapshot call per location run; map `customerId` → local customer via `customers.dutchie_customer_id` (batch the lookup in 1000-row pages); upsert `loyalty_balances` with `current_points = loyaltyBalance`, `lifetime_points = loyaltyEarned`, `enrolled_at` supplied on insert (now()), onConflict `customer_id,organization_id`, deduped 1000-row chunks; skip-and-count unmatched customerIds; update `last_synced_loyalty_at`.
- Rate limit: NEVER call the snapshot more than once per sync run; if `last_synced_loyalty_at` < 20h ago, still allow manual re-sync but log a freshness note (data refreshes nightly upstream).
- configLoader + types + `/api/dutchie/sync` VALID_ENTITY_TYPES + settings UI: add `loyalty` entity tile with its own sync button + timestamp, matching existing tiles.
- Fix the existing `syncTransactions` configKey mismatch (UI references a config field that doesn't exist in DutchieLocationConfig).

B2. **Sync engine quality pass**
- Incremental sync: entities supporting `fromLastModifiedDateUTC` (customers, products) must use it when a last-synced timestamp exists; transactions chunk 55-day windows; inventory pages Skip/Take.
- Single-flight guard: prevent two concurrent syncs for the same location+entity (in-memory lock is acceptable for single-instance dev; note Vercel multi-instance caveat in code comment).
- Error handling: per-record errors must not abort the batch; batch upserts deduped by conflict key; every path writes a complete `dutchie_sync_log` row (no orphaned 'running' rows — add a finally/catch that closes the log as failed).
- Performance: no per-record awaited queries in loops (batch lookups); BATCH_SIZE consistency.

Acceptance criteria:
- AC-B1: Loyalty entity syncs end-to-end on dev: snapshot fetched once, balances upserted, unmatched counted, timestamp updated, sync_log row complete. (Fable will live-verify against dev DB.)
- AC-B2: `loyalty` appears in settings UI with working per-entity sync + last-synced display.
- AC-B3: `syncTransactions` config mismatch fixed; all entity toggles round-trip (save → reload → persisted).
- AC-B4: Customers + products syncs use incremental `fromLastModifiedDateUTC` when available.
- AC-B5: No sync path can leave a `dutchie_sync_log` row stuck in 'running'.
- AC-B6: Concurrent duplicate sync for same location+entity is rejected with 409.

## Phase C — Universal theme system ("theme switch, not recode")

Architecture (Tailwind v4, already on `@theme inline`):
- `globals.css`: semantic token layer defined on `:root` (default = oasis-dark) and `[data-theme="oasis-light"]` (and future themes as new blocks ONLY). Tokens (CSS custom properties): 
  - Surfaces: `--bg`, `--surface`, `--surface-raised`, `--surface-overlay`
  - Borders: `--edge`, `--edge-strong`
  - Text: `--text-primary`, `--text-secondary`, `--text-muted`, `--text-inverse`
  - Brand: `--accent`, `--accent-hover`, `--accent-fg`, `--accent-soft`
  - Status: `--success`, `--warning`, `--danger`, `--info` + `-soft` surface variants
  - Charts: `--chart-1..6`; Focus: `--ring`; plus `--radius-*`, `--shadow-*`
- Map tokens via `@theme inline` to Tailwind utilities: `bg-surface`, `text-muted`, `border-edge`, `bg-accent`, etc.
- ThemeProvider: sets `data-theme` on `<html>`; persisted in cookie + localStorage; inline no-FOUC script in root layout; theme picker UI in Settings → Appearance showing live preview swatches.
- Design language (from Mobbin refs — Supabase Studio calm-neutral dark + Lovable KPI cards): quieter borders, consistent radius, KPI stat cards with trend chips, refined table density. Applied by restyling SHARED components (DataTable, cards, buttons, inputs, modals, Sidebar, headers) — pages inherit.
- Codemod: replace hardcoded `gray-*`/`emerald-*`/`zinc-*` palette classes across all 144 affected files with semantic utilities. Charts read `--chart-*` vars.

Acceptance criteria:
- AC-C1: Zero hardcoded gray/emerald/zinc palette classes remain in `src/app` + `src/components` (grep gate = 0 matches, excluding globals.css itself).
- AC-C2: Switching theme in Settings instantly restyles terminal, backoffice, and storefront with no reload artifacts or FOUC on refresh.
- AC-C3: Adding a demo third theme (`oasis-contrast`, included) requires ONLY a new CSS block — no TSX changes. Its existence proves the contract.
- AC-C4: Default look remains dark+emerald; visual hierarchy per the design language above; WCAG AA contrast for text tokens in both shipped themes.
- AC-C5: Recharts components consume chart tokens (no hex literals in chart code).

## The Rule

**Invoke relevant or requested skills BEFORE any response or action** â€” including clarifying questions, exploring the codebase, or checking files. If it turns out wrong for the situation, you don't have to use it.

**Before entering plan mode:** if you haven't already brainstormed, invoke the brainstorming skill first.

Then announce "Using [skill] to [purpose]" and follow the skill exactly. If it has a checklist, create a todo per item.

## Skill Priority

When multiple skills apply, process skills come first â€” they set the approach, then implementation skills (frontend-design, etc.) carry it out. Brainstorming and systematic-debugging are Superpowers' most common process skills, but the rule holds for any of them.

- "Let's build X" â†’ superpowers:brainstorming first, then implementation skills.
- "Fix this bug" â†’ superpowers:systematic-debugging first, then domain skills.

# The System Architect Auditor

You are operating as a principal-level systems architect with twenty-five-plus years of experience. You have led architecture at SaaS companies through scaling crises, rewritten codebases that grew faster than their first design could handle, and inherited messes from teams that shipped fast and never paid down debt. You know the difference between code that works and code that scales, between code that scales and code that survives an incident at 3 AM. Your job here is to look at an existing system, end to end, and tell the builder exactly what is wrong, what is at risk, and what to fix in what order.

You are not a teacher. You are an auditor. You speak directly. You name the bottleneck. You estimate the blast radius. You name the fix.

## Core Operating Principles

### Audits Find Problems, Not Validation
The user did not bring you in to be told the system is great. If the system has problems, your job is to find them and rank them. If you cannot find problems, the user did not get value from you. Default posture is skeptical. Default tone is direct.

### The System is What is Deployed, Not What Was Designed
Read the actual code. Read the actual schema. Read the actual deployment. Do not audit the README or the architecture diagram. Diagrams are aspirational; production is real. When the diagram and the code disagree, the code wins.

### Every Bottleneck Has a Cost and a Fix
For every issue you find, name three things:
1. The cost: what fails, when, and how loudly.
2. The fix: the smallest change that resolves the underlying problem (not a workaround).
3. The risk of the fix: what could go wrong during migration, and how to mitigate.

Generic findings ("add caching") are useless. Specific findings ("the matter list query at /api/matters/list does a sequential scan because there is no composite index on (firm_id, status, updated_at); add the index, expect 95th-percentile latency to drop from 1.4s to under 100ms, low-risk online migration") are the work product.

### Severity is a Real Number, Not a Color
Use a tight severity scale:
- **P0 â€” Production-fatal.** Will cause data loss, security breach, ToS violation, regulatory exposure, or a service outage. Fix this week.
- **P1 â€” Adoption-blocking.** Will cause customers to churn, support load to spike, or scaling to fail at the next 10x. Fix this month.
- **P2 â€” Drag.** Slows the team, creates noise, or compounds debt. Fix this quarter.
- **P3 â€” Polish.** Cosmetic or future-proofing. Fix when convenient.

Be honest about severity. Inflating P2s to P0s burns trust. Underrating real risks gets people fired.

## What to Look At, in Order

### Step 1: Establish Ground Truth
Before forming any opinion, establish:

1. **Repo layout.** Where does the code live? Is it a monorepo, polyrepo, or a single Next.js app? What packages, what apps, what shared libs?
2. **Stack.** Read `package.json`, `next.config.js`, `tsconfig.json`, Supabase config, `.env.example`, deployment config (`vercel.json`). Confirm versions of Next.js, React, Node, Postgres, Supabase, any AI SDK.
3. **Entry points.** Where does the application boot? What pages exist? What API routes? What edge functions? What background jobs (cron, queue workers, webhooks)?
4. **Data model.** Read the migrations or the schema dump. Map every table, every relationship, every index, every RLS policy.
5. **External integrations.** What third-party services does the system call? Microsoft Graph, OpenAI, Anthropic, S3, Resend, Stripe, etc. How is auth handled for each? Where are secrets stored?
6. **Deployment topology.** Vercel project structure, edge vs. serverless functions, regions, env vars, build configuration.
7. **Observability.** What logs are emitted? Where do they go? What metrics, what alerts, what dashboards?

Until you have all of the above, you are guessing. Do not ship recommendations until you have read enough to actually know.

### Step 2: Trace the Critical Paths
For any meaningful audit, trace at least three critical user-visible paths end to end. For each path:

1. The HTTP request that starts it.
2. The Next.js route handler or server component.
3. The validations and middleware.
4. The Supabase queries (capture every read and write).
5. The external service calls (capture every API call).
6. The response shape returned.
7. The downstream effects (cron triggered, webhook fired, queue enqueued, audit log written).

Walking the path catches what individual file review misses: N+1 queries, repeated external calls, race conditions, incomplete error handling, missing transactions, and the gap between what the front end thinks happened and what the database recorded.

### Step 3: Audit the Data Model
The data model is the substrate. If it is wrong, nothing on top of it can be right. Look for:

1. **Missing primary keys, foreign keys, or constraints.** Every table needs a primary key, every reference needs a foreign key, every required column needs a NOT NULL.
2. **Wrong column types.** Dates stored as strings, money stored as floats, booleans stored as varchar, IDs stored as bigint when they are UUIDs.
3. **Missing or wrong indexes.** Read the queries. Every WHERE, ORDER BY, and JOIN should hit an index. Composite indexes should match query order.
4. **Multi-tenant boundaries.** If this is a multi-tenant app (and a law firm SaaS is), every row needs a tenant column and every query needs a tenant filter. RLS should enforce this at the database, not in application code alone.
5. **Soft delete vs. hard delete.** Mixed strategies create data integrity problems. Pick one and enforce it.
6. **Audit trail.** Every mutation that touches a regulated or auditable record (matter, document, deadline, communication) should leave an immutable audit row.
7. **Vector / embedding tables.** If RAG is involved, look at chunking strategy, embedding dimension, index type (IVFFlat vs. HNSW), and how source-of-record links back from chunks to documents.
8. **Migrations.** Are migrations idempotent? Reversible? Tested in CI? Squashed sensibly? Or is the migration history a 200-file landfill?

### Step 4: Audit the API Surface
Look at every API route and Edge Function. For each:

1. **Auth.** What authenticates the caller? Session? JWT? API key? Are protected routes actually protected?
2. **Authorization.** Who can see what? Who can mutate what? Is authorization centralized or scattered?
3. **Input validation.** Is every input validated at the boundary with Zod or similar? Or do we trust whatever the client sent?
4. **Error handling.** Does the route fail safely? Does it leak stack traces? Does it return consistent shapes?
5. **Idempotency.** Mutations that may be retried (webhooks, payment captures, queue handlers) need idempotency keys.
6. **Transactions.** Multi-step mutations that must be atomic must be in a transaction. Half-applied state is a bug factory.
7. **Rate limiting.** Anything that calls a paid external API needs a rate limit and a per-tenant quota.
8. **Logging.** Each route should log with a correlation ID, the tenant ID, the actor, and the outcome.

### Step 5: Audit the Background Work
Background work is where systems go to die in silence. Look at:

1. **Schedulers.** Vercel cron, Supabase scheduled triggers, external schedulers. What runs, how often, with what error handling?
2. **Webhook receivers.** Are signatures verified? Are duplicate deliveries handled? Are retries idempotent?
3. **Queues.** If there is a queue (pg_boss, Inngest, QStash, Trigger.dev), inspect retry policy, dead-letter handling, and visibility timeout. If there is no queue and there should be, flag it.
4. **Long-running jobs.** Anything that may exceed function timeout (Vercel serverless = 10s on hobby, 60s on pro, 300s on enterprise; edge ~30s) needs a queue or background worker. Inline long-running jobs are a P0 finding.

### Step 6: Audit the Security Posture
Beyond auth/authorization in the API audit:

1. **Secrets.** Are secrets in env vars, not code? Are they scoped per environment? Is rotation possible without downtime?
2. **CORS and CSRF.** Are origins explicit? Is CSRF protection in place for cookie-auth flows?
3. **Content Security Policy.** Is there a real CSP? Or is it `unsafe-inline` everywhere?
4. **Supabase RLS.** Is RLS on for every table that should have it? Have policies been tested with `select`, `insert`, `update`, `delete` at the user role, not just service role?
5. **PII handling.** Where does PII live? Is it encrypted at rest beyond default? Are there fields that should be hashed or tokenized rather than stored plaintext?
6. **Logging hygiene.** Are tokens, secrets, or PII appearing in logs? They will be, somewhere; find it.
7. **Third-party data sharing.** Every external API call is a data-sharing event. Is there a DPA in place? Is the user informed?

### Step 7: Audit the Front End
Front-end audits should not get lost in styling. Focus on:

1. **State management strategy.** Is server state managed with React Query / SWR / RSC properly, or is everything in `useEffect`?
2. **Hydration and waterfalls.** Are there client-side fetch waterfalls that should be server components or `Promise.all`'d?
3. **Bundle size.** What is the largest bundle? What is shipped to every page? Are there imports of `lodash` instead of `lodash/get`?
4. **Accessibility.** Real accessibility, not lip service. Keyboard navigation, focus management, ARIA roles where appropriate.
5. **Loading and error states.** Does every async component have a defined loading state and a defined error state?
6. **Optimistic UI.** Are mutations optimistic where appropriate, or does the user wait for round-trips?
7. **Repeated patterns.** If the same shape of code appears in five pages, it should be a hook or a component.

### Step 8: Audit the AI / LLM Integration (when present)
If the system uses an LLM:

1. **Model of record.** Which model, which version, pinned where? Drifting model versions silently change product behavior.
2. **Prompt construction.** Is the prompt assembled from versioned templates, or are strings concatenated in handlers?
3. **Token accounting.** Is token usage logged per request, per tenant, per feature? Costs spiral without instrumentation.
4. **Error handling.** Timeouts, rate limits, content filter rejections, malformed JSON outputs. All must be handled.
5. **Hallucination guardrails.** For factual outputs (citations, dates, legal references), is there a verification step or only a confidence display?
6. **Audit trail.** For regulated industries (legal, medical, financial), every AI output that influences a decision must be persisted with the prompt, model, version, and timestamp.
7. **Confidentiality.** Are tenant prompts being sent to a model that retains them? Is there a zero-retention agreement? Is there an explicit user disclosure?
8. **Determinism.** Where temperature should be near zero (extraction, classification), is it? Where it should be higher (drafting), is it?

### Step 9: Audit Observability
You cannot debug what you cannot see. Look for:

1. **Logs.** Structured logs with correlation IDs. Or `console.log` strings that nobody can search.
2. **Metrics.** Latency, error rate, throughput per route. Per tenant if multi-tenant.
3. **Tracing.** OpenTelemetry or equivalent for cross-service requests, especially across Edge Functions, Supabase, and external APIs.
4. **Alerts.** Concrete alerts on real SLOs, not "everything looks ok" dashboards. The alert should page someone, and the someone should have a runbook.
5. **Dashboards.** A single dashboard a developer can pull up at 3 AM and see the state of the system.

## How to Frame Findings

Every finding should follow this structure:

```
## Finding: <one-line title>
Severity: P0 | P1 | P2 | P3
Area: data model / API / frontend / background / security / observability / AI
Location: <file paths, route names, table names>

Observation: <what is actually true in the code today>
Failure mode: <what breaks, when, and how it manifests to the user or operator>
Recommended fix: <smallest change that resolves the root cause>
Migration risk: <what could go wrong during the fix and how to mitigate>
Effort: S (under a day) | M (1â€“3 days) | L (1â€“2 weeks) | XL (multi-sprint)
```

Findings should be concrete enough that an engineer reading the report can open the file and start fixing.

## How to Synthesize the Audit

After collecting findings, synthesize into:

1. **Executive summary.** Three to five sentences, naming the top three risks and the top three opportunities. The reader is a CEO or CTO. Lead with the punchline.
2. **The "fix in order" list.** A prioritized backlog of P0/P1 findings with effort estimates, organized for sequential execution. This is what the team works from.
3. **The "do this differently next time" list.** Architectural patterns the team should adopt going forward to prevent the same class of issues. This is what the team learns from.
4. **The "if I had to start over" sketch.** One paragraph describing the cleanest version of this system. Use this to anchor whether incremental fixes are worth the cost vs. a strategic redesign of a subsystem.

## Response Quality Standards

Every response must:

- Read the actual code before judging it. Do not speculate.
- Be specific. Name the file, the function, the table, the query, the route.
- Estimate severity and effort. The user needs to plan, not just to be alarmed.
- Distinguish must-fix from nice-to-have. Do not turn a polish item into a crisis.
- Take a position. If the user asks "should we use X or Y," answer with the choice and the why.
- Surface unknowns explicitly. If you cannot tell from reading whether a behavior is correct, say so and say what would resolve it (a query plan, a load test, a production trace).
- Never use dashes in written content. Use commas, semicolons, or restructure.

## Subagent dispatch requires multi-agent support

Add to your Codex config (`~/.codex/config.toml`):

```toml
[features]
multi_agent = true
```

This enables `spawn_agent`, `wait_agent`, and `close_agent` for skills like `dispatching-parallel-agents` and `subagent-driven-development`. When using subagent-driven-development, you should always close implementer and reviewer subagents when they have finished all their work.

## Environment Detection

Skills that create worktrees or finish branches should detect their
environment with read-only git commands before proceeding:

```bash
GIT_DIR=$(cd "$(git rev-parse --git-dir)" 2>/dev/null && pwd -P)
GIT_COMMON=$(cd "$(git rev-parse --git-common-dir)" 2>/dev/null && pwd -P)
BRANCH=$(git branch --show-current)
```

- `GIT_DIR != GIT_COMMON` â†’ already in a linked worktree (skip creation)
- `BRANCH` empty â†’ detached HEAD (cannot branch/push/PR from sandbox)

See `using-git-worktrees` Step 0 and `finishing-a-development-branch`
Step 1 for how each skill uses these signals.

## Codex App Finishing

When the sandbox blocks branch/push operations (detached HEAD in an
externally managed worktree), the agent commits all work and informs
the user to use the App's native controls:

- **"Create branch"** â€” names the branch, then commit/push/PR via App UI
- **"Hand off to local"** â€” transfers work to the user's local checkout

The agent can still run tests, stage files, and output suggested branch
names, commit messages, and PR descriptions for the user to copy.

## Required NOT NULL Fields (No Default)

These columns are NOT NULL and have NO default value. You MUST provide a value on INSERT.

### audit_log
- `organization_id` (uuid), `entity_type` (text), `event_type` (text)

### customers
- `organization_id` (uuid)

### employees
- `organization_id` (uuid), `first_name` (text), `last_name` (text), `pin_hash` (text), `role` (text)

### inventory_items
- `product_id` (uuid), `location_id` (uuid)

### manifests
- `organization_id` (uuid), `title` (text)

### online_orders
- `location_id` (uuid), `order_number` (bigint), `customer_name` (text), `customer_phone` (text)

### products
- `organization_id` (uuid), `category_id` (uuid), `name` (text), `slug` (text)

### transaction_lines
- `transaction_id` (uuid), `product_id` (uuid), `product_name` (text), `unit_price` (numeric), `line_total` (numeric)

### transaction_payments
- `transaction_id` (uuid), `payment_method` (text), `amount` (numeric)

### transactions
- `location_id` (uuid), `employee_id` (uuid), `transaction_number` (bigint), `transaction_type` (text)

---

## Rules for Code Generation

1. **Before inserting into any table**, check this file for CHECK constraints on that table. Only use listed values.
2. **Before inserting into any table**, check the NOT NULL section. Provide all required fields.
3. **When adding new CHECK constraint values**, create a database migration to ALTER the constraint FIRST, then use the new value in code.
4. **Zod schemas** for API validation must use `z.enum([...])` with EXACTLY the values from this file, not approximations.
5. **TypeScript types** for constrained fields must use union literal types matching this file exactly.
6. **If you need a value not in this list** (like 'exempt' for testing_status), you MUST add a migration to update the CHECK constraint before writing code that uses it.

## Rules for Code Generation

1. **Before inserting into any table**, check this file for CHECK constraints on that table. Only use listed values.
2. **Before inserting into any table**, check the NOT NULL section. Provide all required fields.
3. **When adding new CHECK constraint values**, create a database migration to ALTER the constraint FIRST, then use the new value in code.
4. **Zod schemas** for API validation must use `z.enum([...])` with EXACTLY the values from this file, not approximations.
5. **TypeScript types** for constrained fields must use union literal types matching this file exactly.
6. **If you need a value not in this list** (like 'exempt' for testing_status), you MUST add a migration to update the CHECK constraint before writing code that uses it.

===== 20260401150000_dutchie_gap_analysis.sql =====
-- Dutchie vs Oasis Gap Analysis migration
-- Adds missing medium-priority columns identified by field-by-field API comparison
-- See: DUTCHIE-VS-OASIS-GAP-ANALYSIS.md

-- PRODUCTS: Add missing medium-priority columns
ALTER TABLE products ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS max_per_transaction INTEGER;
ALTER TABLE products ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS standard_allergens JSONB;
ALTER TABLE products ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS oil_volume NUMERIC(8,3);
ALTER TABLE products ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS serving_size TEXT;
ALTER TABLE products ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS serving_size_per_unit NUMERIC(8,3);
ALTER TABLE products ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS is_coupon BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE;

-- CUSTOMERS: Add missing medium-priority columns
ALTER TABLE customers ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS referral_source TEXT;
ALTER TABLE customers ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS other_referral_source TEXT;
ALTER TABLE customers ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS is_anonymous BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE;
ALTER TABLE customers ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS created_at_location_id UUID REFERENCES locations(id);

-- CUSTOMERS: Temporary migration columns (drop after Dutchie cutover)
ALTER TABLE customers ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS dutchie_customer_id INTEGER;
ALTER TABLE customers ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS springbig_member_id TEXT;
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_customers_dutchie_id ON customers(dutchie_customer_id) WHERE dutchie_customer_id IS NOT NULL;

-- PRODUCTS: Temporary migration column
ALTER TABLE products ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS dutchie_product_id INTEGER;
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_products_dutchie_id ON products(dutchie_product_id) WHERE dutchie_product_id IS NOT NULL;

-- CASH DRAWER DROPS: Add structured adjustment reason
ALTER TABLE cash_drawer_drops ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS adjustment_reason TEXT;

-- DUTCHIE MIGRATION: Location API key storage
-- Stores per-location Dutchie API keys for data migration
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS dutchie_locations (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  location_id UUID REFERENCES locations(id),
  location_name TEXT NOT NULL,
  api_key TEXT NOT NULL,
  dutchie_location_id INTEGER,
  dutchie_location_name TEXT,
  is_active BOOLEAN DEFAULT TRUE,
  last_connected_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  last_sync_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  last_error TEXT,
  created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT now(),
  UNIQUE(location_id)
);

ALTER TABLE dutchie_locations ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY;

-- DUTCHIE MIGRATION: Sync job tracking
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS dutchie_sync_jobs (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  location_id UUID REFERENCES locations(id),
  job_type TEXT NOT NULL CHECK (job_type IN ('full', 'products', 'customers', 'inventory', 'brands', 'vendors', 'strains', 'transactions')),
  status TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending' CHECK (status IN ('pending', 'running', 'completed', 'failed')),
  started_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  completed_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  products_fetched INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  products_created INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  products_updated INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  customers_fetched INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  customers_created INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  customers_updated INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  customers_skipped_dupes INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  inventory_fetched INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  inventory_created INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  lookups_created JSONB DEFAULT '{}',
  error_count INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  errors JSONB DEFAULT '[]',
  created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT now()
);

ALTER TABLE dutchie_sync_jobs ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY;
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_dutchie_sync_jobs_location ON dutchie_sync_jobs(location_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_dutchie_sync_jobs_status ON dutchie_sync_jobs(status) WHERE status IN ('pending', 'running');

===== 20260402010000_dutchie_live_sync.sql =====
-- Dutchie Live Sync â€” Config, dedup indexes, sync log
-- Replaces migration-only approach with permanent per-location sync infrastructure

-- dutchie_config: per-location sync configuration
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS dutchie_config (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  location_id UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES locations(id),
  is_enabled BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT false,
  api_key_encrypted TEXT,
  dutchie_location_id TEXT,
  dutchie_location_name TEXT,

  -- Per-entity sync timestamps (set to when sync STARTED, not finished)
  last_synced_employees_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  last_synced_customers_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  last_synced_products_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  last_synced_inventory_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  last_synced_rooms_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  last_synced_reference_at TIMESTAMPTZ,

  -- Sync toggles
  sync_employees BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT true,
  sync_customers BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT true,
  sync_products BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT true,
  sync_inventory BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT true,
  sync_rooms BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT true,

  created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  UNIQUE(location_id)
);

ALTER TABLE dutchie_config ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY;

-- Employees: dedup column + unique index
ALTER TABLE employees ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS dutchie_employee_id TEXT;
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_employees_dutchie_uniq
  ON employees(dutchie_employee_id) WHERE dutchie_employee_id IS NOT NULL;

-- Products: unique index on existing dutchie_product_id
DROP INDEX IF EXISTS idx_products_dutchie_id;
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_products_dutchie_uniq
  ON products(dutchie_product_id) WHERE dutchie_product_id IS NOT NULL;

-- Customers: unique index on existing dutchie_customer_id
DROP INDEX IF EXISTS idx_customers_dutchie_id;
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_customers_dutchie_uniq
  ON customers(dutchie_customer_id) WHERE dutchie_customer_id IS NOT NULL;

-- Inventory items: dedup by external_package_id + location
ALTER TABLE inventory_items ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_package_id TEXT;
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_inventory_external_pkg
  ON inventory_items(external_package_id, location_id) WHERE external_package_id IS NOT NULL;

-- Rooms: external_id for Dutchie room matching
ALTER TABLE rooms ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_rooms_external_id
  ON rooms(external_id, location_id) WHERE external_id IS NOT NULL;

-- Registers: external_id for terminal matching
ALTER TABLE registers ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_registers_external_id
  ON registers(external_id, location_id) WHERE external_id IS NOT NULL;

-- Reference entities: external_id columns
ALTER TABLE brands ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;
ALTER TABLE vendors ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;
ALTER TABLE strains ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;
ALTER TABLE pricing_tiers ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;

-- Sync log table
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS dutchie_sync_log (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  location_id UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES locations(id),
  entity_type TEXT NOT NULL,
  sync_type TEXT NOT NULL CHECK (sync_type IN ('full', 'incremental')),
  status TEXT NOT NULL CHECK (status IN ('running', 'completed', 'failed')) DEFAULT 'running',
  records_fetched INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  records_created INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  records_updated INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  records_skipped INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  records_errored INTEGER DEFAULT 0,
  error_details TEXT[],
  started_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  completed_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  duration_ms INTEGER
);

ALTER TABLE dutchie_sync_log ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY;
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_dutchie_sync_log_location ON dutchie_sync_log(location_id, started_at DESC);

-- Seed dutchie_config from existing dutchie_locations data
INSERT INTO dutchie_config (location_id, is_enabled, api_key_encrypted, dutchie_location_id, dutchie_location_name)
SELECT
  dl.location_id,
  dl.is_active,
  dl.api_key,
  dl.dutchie_location_id::text,
  dl.dutchie_location_name
FROM dutchie_locations dl
WHERE dl.location_id IS NOT NULL
ON CONFLICT (location_id) DO UPDATE SET
  api_key_encrypted = EXCLUDED.api_key_encrypted,
  is_enabled = EXCLUDED.is_enabled;

===== 20260402120000_dutchie_external_ids.sql =====
-- Add external_id to reference tables for Dutchie sync FK resolution
ALTER TABLE brands ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;
ALTER TABLE strains ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;
ALTER TABLE vendors ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;
ALTER TABLE product_categories ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;
ALTER TABLE tags ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;
ALTER TABLE pricing_tiers ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;
ALTER TABLE registers ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS external_id TEXT;

-- Add dutchie_employee_id to employees
ALTER TABLE employees ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS dutchie_employee_id INTEGER;

-- Unique indexes for upsert conflict resolution
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_brands_org_name ON brands(organization_id, name);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_strains_org_name ON strains(organization_id, name);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_vendors_org_name ON vendors(organization_id, name);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_tags_org_name ON tags(organization_id, name, tag_type);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_pricing_tiers_org_name ON pricing_tiers(organization_id, name);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_registers_loc_ext ON registers(location_id, external_id) WHERE external_id IS NOT NULL;
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_employees_org_dutchie ON employees(organization_id, dutchie_employee_id) WHERE dutchie_employee_id IS NOT NULL;

===== 20260402130000_dutchie_upsert_constraints.sql =====
-- Add non-partial unique constraints for Dutchie sync upserts.
-- PostgREST ON CONFLICT requires real constraints, not partial indexes.

-- Employees: upsert by dutchie_employee_id per org
ALTER TABLE employees
  ADD CONSTRAINT employees_org_dutchie_emp_key
  UNIQUE (organization_id, dutchie_employee_id);

-- Customers: upsert by dutchie_customer_id per org
ALTER TABLE customers
  ADD CONSTRAINT customers_org_dutchie_cust_key
  UNIQUE (organization_id, dutchie_customer_id);

-- Products: upsert by dutchie_product_id per org
ALTER TABLE products
  ADD CONSTRAINT products_org_dutchie_prod_key
  UNIQUE (organization_id, dutchie_product_id);

-- Inventory: upsert by external_package_id per location
ALTER TABLE inventory_items
  ADD CONSTRAINT inventory_items_loc_ext_pkg_key
  UNIQUE (location_id, external_package_id);

===== 20260402140000_dutchie_sync_fixes.sql =====
-- Make product_id nullable on inventory_items.
-- During Dutchie sync, inventory may arrive before products are synced.
-- The FK is resolved post-sync or on subsequent product sync.
ALTER TABLE inventory_items ALTER COLUMN product_id DROP NOT NULL;

-- Reload PostgREST schema cache to pick up new constraints from prior migration
NOTIFY pgrst, 'reload schema';

===== 20260402150000_dutchie_transaction_sync.sql =====
-- Add dutchie_transaction_id for upsert conflict resolution
ALTER TABLE transactions ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS dutchie_transaction_id TEXT;

-- Make employee_id nullable for Dutchie imports (employee may not be synced yet)
ALTER TABLE transactions ALTER COLUMN employee_id DROP NOT NULL;

-- Unique constraint for upsert (non-partial so PostgREST can use it)
ALTER TABLE transactions
  ADD CONSTRAINT transactions_loc_dutchie_txn_key
  UNIQUE (location_id, dutchie_transaction_id);

-- Reload PostgREST schema cache
NOTIFY pgrst, 'reload schema';

===== src/lib/dutchie/configLoader.ts =====
    1: import { createSupabaseServerClient } from '@/lib/supabase/server'
    2: 
    3: export interface DutchieLocationConfig {
    4:   locationId: string
    5:   isEnabled: boolean
    6:   apiKey: string
    7:   dutchieLocationId: string | null
    8:   dutchieLocationName: string | null
    9:   syncEmployees: boolean
   10:   syncCustomers: boolean
   11:   syncProducts: boolean
   12:   syncInventory: boolean
   13:   syncRooms: boolean
   14:   lastSyncedEmployeesAt: Date | null
   15:   lastSyncedCustomersAt: Date | null
   16:   lastSyncedProductsAt: Date | null
   17:   lastSyncedInventoryAt: Date | null
   18:   lastSyncedRoomsAt: Date | null
   19:   lastSyncedReferenceAt: Date | null
   20:   lastSyncedTransactionsAt: Date | null
   21: }
   22: 
   23: const cache = new Map<string, { config: DutchieLocationConfig; timestamp: number }>()
   24: const CACHE_TTL = 5 * 60 * 1000
   25: 
   26: export async function loadDutchieConfig(locationId: string): Promise<DutchieLocationConfig | null> {
   27:   const cached = cache.get(locationId)
   28:   if (cached && Date.now() - cached.timestamp < CACHE_TTL) return cached.config
   29: 
   30:   const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
   31:   const { data } = await (sb as any).from('dutchie_config')
   32:     .select('*')
   33:     .eq('location_id', locationId)
   34:     .maybeSingle()
   35: 
   36:   if (!data) return null
   37: 
   38:   const config: DutchieLocationConfig = {
   39:     locationId: data.location_id,
   40:     isEnabled: data.is_enabled,
   41:     apiKey: data.api_key_encrypted || '',
   42:     dutchieLocationId: data.dutchie_location_id,
   43:     dutchieLocationName: data.dutchie_location_name,
   44:     syncEmployees: data.sync_employees,
   45:     syncCustomers: data.sync_customers,
   46:     syncProducts: data.sync_products,
   47:     syncInventory: data.sync_inventory,
   48:     syncRooms: data.sync_rooms,
   49:     lastSyncedEmployeesAt: data.last_synced_employees_at ? new Date(data.last_synced_employees_at) : null,
   50:     lastSyncedCustomersAt: data.last_synced_customers_at ? new Date(data.last_synced_customers_at) : null,
   51:     lastSyncedProductsAt: data.last_synced_products_at ? new Date(data.last_synced_products_at) : null,
   52:     lastSyncedInventoryAt: data.last_synced_inventory_at ? new Date(data.last_synced_inventory_at) : null,
   53:     lastSyncedRoomsAt: data.last_synced_rooms_at ? new Date(data.last_synced_rooms_at) : null,
   54:     lastSyncedReferenceAt: data.last_synced_reference_at ? new Date(data.last_synced_reference_at) : null,
   55:     lastSyncedTransactionsAt: data.last_synced_transactions_at ? new Date(data.last_synced_transactions_at) : null,
   56:   }
   57: 
   58:   cache.set(locationId, { config, timestamp: Date.now() })
   59:   return config
   60: }
   61: 
   62: export function clearDutchieConfigCache(locationId?: string): void {
   63:   if (locationId) cache.delete(locationId)
   64:   else cache.clear()
   65: }
   66: 
   67: export async function updateSyncTimestamp(
   68:   locationId: string,
   69:   entityType: 'employees' | 'customers' | 'products' | 'inventory' | 'rooms' | 'reference' | 'transactions',
   70:   timestamp: Date,
   71: ): Promise<void> {
   72:   const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
   73:   const col = `last_synced_${entityType}_at`
   74:   await (sb as any).from('dutchie_config')
   75:     .update({ [col]: timestamp.toISOString() })
   76:     .eq('location_id', locationId)
   77:   clearDutchieConfigCache(locationId)
   78: }

===== src/app/api/dutchie/sync/route.ts =====
    1: import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'
    2: import { requireSession } from '@/lib/auth/session'
    3: import { loadDutchieConfig } from '@/lib/dutchie/configLoader'
    4: import { DutchieClient } from '@/lib/dutchie/client'
    5: import { syncLocation } from '@/lib/dutchie/syncEngine'
    6: import { logger } from '@/lib/utils/logger'
    7: import type { EntityType } from '@/lib/dutchie/types'
    8: 
    9: /**
   10:  * POST /api/dutchie/sync
   11:  * Triggers a live sync from Dutchie for the session's location.
   12:  *
   13:  * Body:
   14:  * - entityTypes?: string[] â€” which entity types to sync (default: all enabled)
   15:  *
   16:  * Delegates to syncEngine which handles fetch, mapping, upsert, and logging.
   17:  */
   18: 
   19: const VALID_ENTITY_TYPES: EntityType[] = ['employees', 'customers', 'products', 'inventory', 'rooms', 'transactions']
   20: 
   21: export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
   22:   try {
   23:     const session = await requireSession()
   24:     const body = await request.json().catch(() => ({}))
   25: 
   26:     // Load config
   27:     const config = await loadDutchieConfig(session.locationId)
   28:     if (!config) {
   29:       return NextResponse.json({ error: 'No Dutchie configuration found for this location' }, { status: 404 })
   30:     }
   31:     if (!config.apiKey) {
   32:       return NextResponse.json({ error: 'No API key configured' }, { status: 400 })
   33:     }
   34: 
   35:     // Validate connection
   36:     const client = new DutchieClient(config.apiKey)
   37:     const whoami = await client.whoami()
   38:     logger.info('Dutchie whoami result', {
   39:       locationName: whoami.locationName,
   40:       locationId: whoami.locationId,
   41:       companyName: whoami.companyName,
   42:       valid: whoami.valid,
   43:       oasisLocationId: session.locationId,
   44:     })
   45:     if (!whoami.valid) {
   46:       return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid API key or connection failed' }, { status: 400 })
   47:     }
   48: 
   49:     // Determine which entity types to sync
   50:     let entityTypes: EntityType[] | undefined
   51:     if (body.entityTypes && Array.isArray(body.entityTypes)) {
   52:       entityTypes = body.entityTypes.filter((t: string) =>
   53:         VALID_ENTITY_TYPES.includes(t as EntityType),
   54:       ) as EntityType[]
   55:       if (entityTypes.length === 0) {
   56:         return NextResponse.json({ error: 'No valid entity types specified' }, { status: 400 })
   57:       }
   58:     }
   59: 
   60:     // Delegate to sync engine â€” handles fetch, mapping, upsert, soft-delete, and logging
   61:     const locationResult = await syncLocation(session.locationId, session.organizationId, entityTypes)
   62: 
   63:     const results = locationResult.results.map(r => ({
   64:       entityType: r.entityType,
   65:       fetched: r.fetched,
   66:       created: r.created,
   67:       updated: r.updated,
   68:       skipped: r.skipped,
   69:       errors: r.errored,
   70:       duration: r.durationMs,
   71:     }))
   72: 
   73:     const allErrors = locationResult.results.flatMap(r => r.errors)
   74: 
   75:     logger.info('Dutchie sync complete', {
   76:       locationId: session.locationId,
   77:       entityTypes: locationResult.results.map(r => r.entityType),
   78:       duration: locationResult.totalDurationMs,
   79:       errorCount: allErrors.length,
   80:     })
   81: 
   82:     return NextResponse.json({ results, errors: allErrors.slice(0, 50) })
   83:   } catch (err) {
   84:     if (err && typeof err === 'object' && 'code' in err) {
   85:       const a = err as { code: string; statusCode?: number }
   86:       if (a.code === 'UNAUTHORIZED') return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Auth required' }, { status: 401 })
   87:     }
   88:     logger.error('Dutchie sync error', { error: String(err) })
   89:     return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Server error' }, { status: 500 })
   90:   }
   91: }
===== src/app/api/dutchie/sync/log/route.ts =====
    1: import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'
    2: import { requireSession } from '@/lib/auth/session'
    3: import { createSupabaseServerClient } from '@/lib/supabase/server'
    4: import { logger } from '@/lib/utils/logger'
    5: 
    6: /**
    7:  * GET /api/dutchie/sync/log
    8:  * Returns recent dutchie_sync_log entries.
    9:  * Filters by session location if available, otherwise returns all.
   10:  * Supports ?limit=20 (default 20, max 100).
   11:  */
   12: export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {
   13:   try {
   14:     const session = await requireSession()
   15:     const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
   16: 
   17:     const url = request.nextUrl
   18:     const limitParam = parseInt(url.searchParams.get('limit') ?? '20', 10)
   19:     const limit = Math.min(Math.max(limitParam, 1), 100)
   20: 
   21:     // eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any
   22:     let query = (sb as any).from('dutchie_sync_log')
   23:       .select('*')
   24:       .order('started_at', { ascending: false })
   25:       .limit(limit)
   26: 
   27:     // Only filter by location if one is selected
   28:     if (session.locationId) {
   29:       query = query.eq('location_id', session.locationId)
   30:     }
   31: 
   32:     const { data: logs, error } = await query
   33: 
   34:     if (error) {
   35:       logger.error('Dutchie sync log query error', { error: error.message })
   36:       return NextResponse.json({ logs: [] })
   37:     }
   38: 
   39:     return NextResponse.json({ logs: logs ?? [] })
   40:   } catch (err) {
   41:     // If auth fails, return empty logs instead of 500
   42:     if (err && typeof err === 'object' && 'code' in err) {
   43:       const appErr = err as { code: string }
   44:       if (appErr.code === 'UNAUTHORIZED') {
   45:         return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Authentication required' }, { status: 401 })
   46:       }
   47:     }
   48:     logger.error('Dutchie sync log error', { error: String(err) })
   49:     // Return empty array instead of 500 â€” this is a non-critical read
   50:     return NextResponse.json({ logs: [] })
   51:   }
   52: }
===== src/app/api/settings/dutchie-config/route.ts =====
    1: import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'
    2: import { z } from 'zod/v4'
    3: import { requireSession } from '@/lib/auth/session'
    4: import { createSupabaseServerClient } from '@/lib/supabase/server'
    5: import { clearDutchieConfigCache } from '@/lib/dutchie/configLoader'
    6: import { logger } from '@/lib/utils/logger'
    7: 
    8: const UpdateDutchieConfigSchema = z.object({
    9:   isEnabled: z.boolean().optional(),
   10:   apiKey: z.string().optional(),
   11:   syncEmployees: z.boolean().optional(),
   12:   syncCustomers: z.boolean().optional(),
   13:   syncProducts: z.boolean().optional(),
   14:   syncInventory: z.boolean().optional(),
   15:   syncRooms: z.boolean().optional(),
   16: })
   17: 
   18: const DEFAULT_CONFIG = {
   19:   isEnabled: false,
   20:   apiKey: '',
   21:   dutchieLocationId: '',
   22:   dutchieLocationName: '',
   23:   syncEmployees: true,
   24:   syncCustomers: true,
   25:   syncProducts: true,
   26:   syncInventory: true,
   27:   syncRooms: true,
   28:   lastSyncedEmployeesAt: null as string | null,
   29:   lastSyncedCustomersAt: null as string | null,
   30:   lastSyncedProductsAt: null as string | null,
   31:   lastSyncedInventoryAt: null as string | null,
   32:   lastSyncedRoomsAt: null as string | null,
   33:   lastSyncedReferenceAt: null as string | null,
   34: }
   35: 
   36: /** Mask API key: show last 4 chars as ****...xxxx */
   37: function maskApiKey(key: string | null): string {
   38:   if (!key || key.length < 4) return ''
   39:   return '****...' + key.slice(-4)
   40: }
   41: 
   42: /** Map DB row to frontend camelCase */
   43: function dbRowToFrontend(row: Record<string, unknown>) {
   44:   const rawKey = (row.api_key_encrypted as string) ?? ''
   45:   return {
   46:     isEnabled: row.is_enabled ?? DEFAULT_CONFIG.isEnabled,
   47:     apiKey: maskApiKey(rawKey),
   48:     dutchieLocationId: (row.dutchie_location_id as string) ?? '',
   49:     dutchieLocationName: (row.dutchie_location_name as string) ?? '',
   50:     syncEmployees: row.sync_employees ?? DEFAULT_CONFIG.syncEmployees,
   51:     syncCustomers: row.sync_customers ?? DEFAULT_CONFIG.syncCustomers,
   52:     syncProducts: row.sync_products ?? DEFAULT_CONFIG.syncProducts,
   53:     syncInventory: row.sync_inventory ?? DEFAULT_CONFIG.syncInventory,
   54:     syncRooms: row.sync_rooms ?? DEFAULT_CONFIG.syncRooms,
   55:     lastSyncedEmployeesAt: (row.last_synced_employees_at as string) ?? null,
   56:     lastSyncedCustomersAt: (row.last_synced_customers_at as string) ?? null,
   57:     lastSyncedProductsAt: (row.last_synced_products_at as string) ?? null,
   58:     lastSyncedInventoryAt: (row.last_synced_inventory_at as string) ?? null,
   59:     lastSyncedRoomsAt: (row.last_synced_rooms_at as string) ?? null,
   60:     lastSyncedReferenceAt: (row.last_synced_reference_at as string) ?? null,
   61:   }
   62: }
   63: 
   64: /** Map frontend camelCase to DB snake_case for upsert */
   65: function frontendToDbRow(data: Record<string, unknown>, locationId: string) {
   66:   const row: Record<string, unknown> = { location_id: locationId, updated_at: new Date().toISOString() }
   67: 
   68:   if (data.isEnabled !== undefined) row.is_enabled = data.isEnabled
   69:   if (data.syncEmployees !== undefined) row.sync_employees = data.syncEmployees
   70:   if (data.syncCustomers !== undefined) row.sync_customers = data.syncCustomers
   71:   if (data.syncProducts !== undefined) row.sync_products = data.syncProducts
   72:   if (data.syncInventory !== undefined) row.sync_inventory = data.syncInventory
   73:   if (data.syncRooms !== undefined) row.sync_rooms = data.syncRooms
   74: 
   75:   // Only update API key if it's a real value (not the masked version)
   76:   if (data.apiKey !== undefined && typeof data.apiKey === 'string' && !data.apiKey.startsWith('****')) {
   77:     row.api_key_encrypted = data.apiKey
   78:   }
   79: 
   80:   return row
   81: }
   82: 
   83: export async function GET() {
   84:   try {
   85:     const session = await requireSession()
   86:     const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
   87: 
   88:     const { data: config, error } = await (sb as any).from('dutchie_config')
   89:       .select('*')
   90:       .eq('location_id', session.locationId)
   91:       .maybeSingle()
   92: 
   93:     if (error) return NextResponse.json({ error: error.message }, { status: 500 })
   94: 
   95:     return NextResponse.json({
   96:       config: config ? dbRowToFrontend(config) : DEFAULT_CONFIG,
   97:     })
   98:   } catch (err) {
   99:     if (err && typeof err === 'object' && 'code' in err) {
  100:       const appErr = err as { code: string; message: string; statusCode?: number }
  101:       if (appErr.code === 'UNAUTHORIZED') return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Authentication required' }, { status: 401 })
  102:       return NextResponse.json({ error: appErr.message }, { status: appErr.statusCode ?? 500 })
  103:     }
  104:     logger.error('Dutchie config get error', { error: String(err) })
  105:     return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Server error' }, { status: 500 })
  106:   }
  107: }
  108: 
  109: export async function PATCH(request: NextRequest) {
  110:   try {
  111:     const session = await requireSession()
  112:     const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
  113:     const body = await request.json()
  114:     const parsed = UpdateDutchieConfigSchema.safeParse(body)
  115: 
  116:     if (!parsed.success) {
  117:       return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid input', details: parsed.error.issues }, { status: 400 })
  118:     }
  119: 
  120:     const dbRow = frontendToDbRow(parsed.data as Record<string, unknown>, session.locationId)
  121: 
  122:     const { data: config, error } = await (sb as any).from('dutchie_config')
  123:       .upsert(dbRow, { onConflict: 'location_id' })
  124:       .select()
  125:       .single()
  126: 
  127:     if (error) return NextResponse.json({ error: error.message }, { status: 500 })
  128: 
  129:     clearDutchieConfigCache(session.locationId)
  130: 
  131:     return NextResponse.json({ config: dbRowToFrontend(config) })
  132:   } catch (err) {
  133:     if (err && typeof err === 'object' && 'code' in err) {
  134:       const appErr = err as { code: string; message: string; statusCode?: number }
  135:       if (appErr.code === 'UNAUTHORIZED') return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Authentication required' }, { status: 401 })
  136:       return NextResponse.json({ error: appErr.message }, { status: appErr.statusCode ?? 500 })
  137:     }
  138:     logger.error('Dutchie config update error', { error: String(err) })
  139:     return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Server error' }, { status: 500 })
  140:   }
  141: }

===== src/lib/auth/session.ts =====
    1: import { SignJWT, jwtVerify } from 'jose'
    2: import { cookies } from 'next/headers'
    3: import { AppError } from '@/lib/utils/errors'
    4: 
    5: export interface SessionPayload {
    6:   employeeId: string
    7:   organizationId: string
    8:   locationId: string
    9:   locationName: string
   10:   employeeName: string
   11:   role: 'budtender' | 'shift_lead' | 'manager' | 'admin' | 'owner'
   12:   permissions: string[]
   13:   registerId: string
   14:   registerName: string
   15:   exp: number
   16: }
   17: 
   18: const COOKIE_NAME = 'oasis-session'
   19: const SESSION_DURATION_SECONDS = 12 * 60 * 60 // 12 hours
   20: 
   21: function getSecret(): Uint8Array {
   22:   const secret = process.env.SESSION_SECRET
   23:   if (!secret) throw new Error('SESSION_SECRET environment variable is not set')
   24:   return new TextEncoder().encode(secret)
   25: }
   26: 
   27: export async function createSessionToken(payload: Omit<SessionPayload, 'exp'>): Promise<string> {
   28:   const exp = Math.floor(Date.now() / 1000) + SESSION_DURATION_SECONDS
   29:   return new SignJWT({ ...payload, exp } as unknown as Record<string, unknown>)
   30:     .setProtectedHeader({ alg: 'HS256' })
   31:     .setExpirationTime(exp)
   32:     .sign(getSecret())
   33: }
   34: 
   35: export async function createSession(payload: Omit<SessionPayload, 'exp'>): Promise<void> {
   36:   const token = await createSessionToken(payload)
   37:   const cookieStore = await cookies()
   38:   cookieStore.set(COOKIE_NAME, token, {
   39:     httpOnly: true,
   40:     secure: process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production',
   41:     sameSite: 'lax',
   42:     path: '/',
   43:     maxAge: SESSION_DURATION_SECONDS,
   44:   })
   45: }
   46: 
   47: export async function getSession(): Promise<SessionPayload | null> {
   48:   const cookieStore = await cookies()
   49:   const token = cookieStore.get(COOKIE_NAME)?.value
   50:   if (!token) return null
   51: 
   52:   try {
   53:     const { payload } = await jwtVerify(token, getSecret())
   54:     return payload as unknown as SessionPayload
   55:   } catch {
   56:     return null
   57:   }
   58: }
   59: 
   60: export async function destroySession(): Promise<void> {
   61:   const cookieStore = await cookies()
   62:   cookieStore.set(COOKIE_NAME, '', {
   63:     httpOnly: true,
   64:     secure: process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production',
   65:     sameSite: 'lax',
   66:     path: '/',
   67:     maxAge: 0,
   68:   })
   69: }
   70: 
   71: export async function requireSession(): Promise<SessionPayload> {
   72:   const session = await getSession()
   73:   if (!session) {
   74:     throw new AppError('UNAUTHORIZED', 'Authentication required', undefined, 401)
   75:   }
   76: 
   77:   // Check for location override from the backoffice location switcher
   78:   const cookieStore = await cookies()
   79:   const locationOverride = cookieStore.get('oasis-location-id')?.value
   80:   if (locationOverride && locationOverride !== session.locationId) {

   82:     return {
   83:       ...session,
   84:       locationId: locationOverride,
   85:       locationName: locationName ?? session.locationName,
   86:     }
   87:   }
   88: 
   89:   return session
   90: }

    1: import { createSupabaseServerClient } from '@/lib/supabase/server'
    2: import { logger } from '@/lib/utils/logger'

    7: import { mapProduct } from './mappers/productMapper'
    8: import { mapInventoryItem } from './mappers/inventoryMapper'

   10: import { mapTransaction } from './mappers/transactionMapper'

   12:   mapBrand, mapStrain, mapVendor, mapCategory,
   13:   mapTag, mapPricingTier, mapTerminal,
   14: } from './mappers/referenceMapper'
   15: import type { SyncResult, LocationSyncResult, EntityType, DutchieProduct, DutchieTransaction } from './types'

   17: const BATCH_SIZE = 1000
   18: 
   19: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   20: // Helpers
   21: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   22: 
   23: function emptySyncResult(entityType: string, syncType: 'full' | 'incremental'): SyncResult {
   24:   return { entityType, syncType, fetched: 0, created: 0, updated: 0, skipped: 0, errored: 0, errors: [], durationMs: 0 }
   25: }
   26: 
   27: async function createSyncLog(
   28:   sb: ReturnType<typeof Object>,
   29:   locationId: string,
   30:   entityType: string,
   31:   syncType: 'full' | 'incremental',
   32: ): Promise<string> {
   33:   const { data } = await (sb as any).from('dutchie_sync_log').insert({
   34:     location_id: locationId,
   35:     entity_type: entityType,
   36:     sync_type: syncType,
   37:     status: 'running',
   38:     started_at: new Date().toISOString(),
   39:   }).select('id').single()
   40:   return data?.id ?? ''
   41: }
   42: 
   43: async function completeSyncLog(
   44:   sb: ReturnType<typeof Object>,
   45:   logId: string,
   46:   result: SyncResult,
   47: ): Promise<void> {
   48:   if (!logId) return
   49:   await (sb as any).from('dutchie_sync_log').update({
   50:     status: result.errored > 0 && result.created + result.updated === 0 ? 'failed' : 'completed',
   51:     completed_at: new Date().toISOString(),
   52:     records_fetched: result.fetched,
   53:     records_created: result.created,
   54:     records_updated: result.updated,
   55:     records_skipped: result.skipped,
   56:     records_errored: result.errored,
   57:     error_details: result.errors.length > 0 ? result.errors : null,
   58:     duration_ms: result.durationMs,
   59:   }).eq('id', logId)
   60: }
   61: 
   62: async function batchUpsert(
   63:   sb: ReturnType<typeof Object>,
   64:   table: string,
   65:   rows: Record<string, unknown>[],
   66:   conflictColumns: string,
   67:   result: SyncResult,
   68: ): Promise<void> {
   69:   // Deduplicate rows by conflict key to avoid "cannot affect row a second time"
   70:   const conflictKeys = conflictColumns.split(',').map(k => k.trim())
   71:   const seen = new Set<string>()
   72:   const deduped: Record<string, unknown>[] = []
   73:   for (let i = rows.length - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
   74:     const key = conflictKeys.map(k => String(rows[i][k] ?? '')).join('|')
   75:     if (seen.has(key)) { result.skipped++; continue }
   76:     seen.add(key)
   77:     deduped.push(rows[i])
   78:   }
   79:   deduped.reverse()
   80: 
   81:   for (let i = 0; i < deduped.length; i += BATCH_SIZE) {
   82:     const batch = deduped.slice(i, i + BATCH_SIZE)
   83:     const { data, error } = await (sb as any).from(table)
   84:       .upsert(batch, { onConflict: conflictColumns, ignoreDuplicates: false })
   85:       .select('id')
   86:     if (error) {
   87:       result.errored += batch.length
   88:       result.errors.push(`${table} batch ${i}: ${error.message}`)
   89:       logger.error('Batch upsert failed', { table, batch: i, error: error.message })
   90:     } else {
   91:       result.updated += data?.length ?? batch.length
   92:     }
   93:   }
   94: }
   95: 
   96: async function getClient(locationId: string): Promise<{ client: DutchieClient; config: Awaited<ReturnType<typeof loadDutchieConfig>> } | null> {
   97:   const config = await loadDutchieConfig(locationId)
   98:   if (!config || !config.isEnabled || !config.apiKey) return null
   99:   return { client: new DutchieClient(config.apiKey), config }
  100: }

  106: export async function syncEmployees(locationId: string, organizationId: string): Promise<SyncResult> {
  107:   const start = Date.now()
  108:   const setup = await getClient(locationId)
  109:   if (!setup) return { ...emptySyncResult('employees', 'full'), durationMs: Date.now() - start }
  110:   const { client, config } = setup
  111: 
  112:   const syncType: 'full' | 'incremental' = config.lastSyncedEmployeesAt ? 'incremental' : 'full'
  113:   const result = emptySyncResult('employees', syncType)
  114:   const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
  115:   const logId = await createSyncLog(sb, locationId, 'employees', syncType)
  116: 
  117:   try {
  118:     const dutchieEmployees = await client.fetchEmployees()
  119:     result.fetched = dutchieEmployees.length
  120: 
  121:     const mapped = dutchieEmployees.map((e) => mapEmployee(e, organizationId))
  122:     const valid = filterValid(mapped, 'dutchie_employee_id', result)
  123: 
  124:     await batchUpsert(sb, 'employees', valid, 'organization_id,dutchie_employee_id', result)
  125:     await syncEmployeeLocations(sb, locationId, organizationId, dutchieEmployees)
  126:   } catch (err) {
  127:     handleSyncError(err, result)
  128:   }
  129: 
  130:   if (result.fetched > 0) {
  131:     await updateSyncTimestamp(locationId, 'employees', new Date(start))
  132:   }
  133: 
  134:   result.durationMs = Date.now() - start
  135:   await completeSyncLog(sb, logId, result)
  136:   logger.info('syncEmployees complete', { locationId, ...result })
  137:   return result
  138: }
  139: 
  140: async function syncEmployeeLocations(
  141:   sb: ReturnType<typeof Object>,
  142:   locationId: string,
  143:   organizationId: string,
  144:   dutchieEmployees: Array<Record<string, unknown>>,
  145: ): Promise<void> {
  146:   const { data: employees } = await (sb as any).from('employees')
  147:     .select('id, dutchie_employee_id')
  148:     .eq('organization_id', organizationId)
  149:     .not('dutchie_employee_id', 'is', null)
  150: 
  151:   if (!employees?.length) return
  152:   // dutchie_employee_id is stored as string in DB
  153:   const idMap = new Map<string, string>()
  154:   for (const emp of employees) {
  155:     idMap.set(String(emp.dutchie_employee_id), emp.id)
  156:   }
  157: 
  158:   const junctionRows = dutchieEmployees
  159:     .map((de) => {
  160:       const dutchieId = String(de.userId ?? de.employeeId ?? '')
  161:       return idMap.has(dutchieId) ? { employee_id: idMap.get(dutchieId), location_id: locationId } : null
  162:     })
  163:     .filter(Boolean)
  164: 
  165:   // Deduplicate by employee_id (Dutchie returns same employee multiple times)
  166:   const seen = new Set<string>()
  167:   const uniqueRows = junctionRows.filter((r) => {
  168:     const eid = (r as { employee_id: string }).employee_id
  169:     if (seen.has(eid)) return false
  170:     seen.add(eid)
  171:     return true
  172:   })
  173: 
  174:   if (uniqueRows.length > 0) {
  175:     await (sb as any).from('employee_locations')
  176:       .upsert(uniqueRows, { onConflict: 'employee_id,location_id', ignoreDuplicates: true })
  177:   }
  178: }

  181: // syncCustomers
  182: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
  183: 
  184: export async function syncCustomers(locationId: string, organizationId: string): Promise<SyncResult> {
  185:   const start = Date.now()
  186:   const setup = await getClient(locationId)
  187:   if (!setup) return { ...emptySyncResult('customers', 'full'), durationMs: Date.now() - start }
  188:   const { client, config } = setup
  189: 
  190:   const syncType: 'full' | 'incremental' = config.lastSyncedCustomersAt ? 'incremental' : 'full'
  191:   const result = emptySyncResult('customers', syncType)
  192:   const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
  193:   const logId = await createSyncLog(sb, locationId, 'customers', syncType)
  194: 
  195:   try {
  196:     const since = config.lastSyncedCustomersAt ?? undefined
  197:     const dutchieCustomers = await client.fetchCustomers(since)
  198:     result.fetched = dutchieCustomers.length
  199: 
  200:     const mapped = dutchieCustomers.map((c) => mapCustomer(c, organizationId))
  201:     const valid = filterValid(mapped, 'dutchie_customer_id', result)
  202: 
  203:     await dedupAndUpsertCustomers(sb, organizationId, valid, result)
  204:   } catch (err) {
  205:     handleSyncError(err, result)
  206:   }
  207: 
  208:   if (result.fetched > 0) {
  209:     await updateSyncTimestamp(locationId, 'customers', new Date(start))
  210:   }
  211: 
  212:   result.durationMs = Date.now() - start
  213:   await completeSyncLog(sb, logId, result)
  214:   logger.info('syncCustomers complete', { locationId, ...result })
  215:   return result
  216: }
  217: 
  218: async function dedupAndUpsertCustomers(
  219:   sb: ReturnType<typeof Object>,
  220:   organizationId: string,
  221:   mapped: Record<string, unknown>[],
  222:   result: SyncResult,
  223: ): Promise<void> {
  224:   // Load existing customers that have email but no dutchie_customer_id
  225:   const emailsToCheck = mapped
  226:     .filter((c) => c.email && !c.dutchie_customer_id)
  227:     .map((c) => c.email as string)
  228: 
  229:   const emailMap = new Map<string, string>()
  230:   if (emailsToCheck.length > 0) {
  231:     const { data: existing } = await (sb as any).from('customers')
  232:       .select('id, email')
  233:       .eq('organization_id', organizationId)
  234:       .is('dutchie_customer_id', null)
  235:       .in('email', emailsToCheck)
  236: 
  237:     for (const row of existing ?? []) {
  238:       if (row.email) emailMap.set(row.email.toLowerCase(), row.id)
  239:     }
  240:   }
  241: 
  242:   // Stamp dutchie_customer_id on email-matched rows
  243:   const toUpdate: Array<{ id: string; dutchie_customer_id: number }> = []
  244:   const toUpsert: Record<string, unknown>[] = []
  245: 
  246:   for (const record of mapped) {
  247:     const email = (record.email as string | null)?.toLowerCase()
  248:     if (email && emailMap.has(email)) {
  249:       toUpdate.push({
  250:         id: emailMap.get(email)!,
  251:         dutchie_customer_id: record.dutchie_customer_id as number,
  252:       })
  253:     }
  254:     toUpsert.push(record)
  255:   }
  256: 
  257:   // Stamp existing email matches
  258:   for (const upd of toUpdate) {
  259:     await (sb as any).from('customers')
  260:       .update({ dutchie_customer_id: upd.dutchie_customer_id })
  261:       .eq('id', upd.id)
  262:   }
  263: 
  264:   // Batch upsert all
  265:   await batchUpsert(sb, 'customers', toUpsert, 'organization_id,dutchie_customer_id', result)
  266: }
  267: 
  268: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
  269: // syncProducts
  270: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
  271: 
  272: export async function syncProducts(locationId: string, organizationId: string): Promise<SyncResult> {
  273:   const start = Date.now()
  274:   const setup = await getClient(locationId)
  275:   if (!setup) return { ...emptySyncResult('products', 'full'), durationMs: Date.now() - start }
  276:   const { client, config } = setup
  277: 
  278:   const syncType: 'full' | 'incremental' = config.lastSyncedProductsAt ? 'incremental' : 'full'
  279:   const result = emptySyncResult('products', syncType)
  280:   const sb = await createSupabaseServerClient()
  281:   const logId = await createSyncLog(sb, locationId, 'products', syncType)
  282: 
  283:   try {
  284:     const since = config.lastSyncedProductsAt ?? undefined
  285:     const dutchieProducts = await client.fetchProducts(since)
  286:     result.fetched = dutchieProducts.length
  287: 
  288:     // Phase 1: resolve FK lookups + pre-create missing FKs in bulk
  289:     const fkCache = await buildProductFkCache(sb, organizationId)
  290:     await bulkResolveNewFks(sb, fkCache, dutchieProducts, organizationId)
  291: 
  292:     // Phase 2: map products (all FK lookups are now in-memory)
  293:     const productRows: Record<string, unknown>[] = []
  294:     const priceRows: Array<{ dutchie_product_id: number; row: Record<string, unknown> }> = []
  295: 
  296:     for (const dp of dutchieProducts) {
  297:       try {
  298:         const { product, locationPrice } = mapProduct(dp, organizationId, locationId)
  299:         product.brand_id = resolveFkSync(fkCache, 'brands', dp.brandName, dp.brandId)
  300:         product.vendor_id = resolveFkSync(fkCache, 'vendors', dp.vendorName, dp.vendorId)
  301:         product.strain_id = resolveFkSync(fkCache, 'strains', dp.strain, dp.strainId)
  302:         product.category_id = resolveCategoryFkSync(fkCache, dp.category, dp.categoryId)
  303:         productRows.push(product as unknown as Record<string, unknown>)
  304:         priceRows.push({ dutchie_product_id: dp.productId, row: locationPrice as unknown as Record<string, unknown> })
  305:       } catch (err) {
  306:         result.errored++
  307:         result.errors.push(`Product ${dp.productId}: ${err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err)}`)
  308:       }
  309:     }
  310: 
  311:     // Phase 2 upsert products
  312:     await batchUpsert(sb, 'products', productRows, 'organization_id,dutchie_product_id', result)
  313: 
  314:     // Phase 3: upsert location_product_prices
  315:     await upsertLocationPrices(sb, organizationId, locationId, priceRows, result)
  316:   } catch (err) {
  317:     handleSyncError(err, result)
  318:   }
  319: 
  320:   // Always save timestamp so next sync is incremental (even if some batches errored)
  321:   if (result.fetched > 0) {
  322:     await updateSyncTimestamp(locationId, 'products', new Date(start))
  323:   }
  324: 
  325:   result.durationMs = Date.now() - start
  326:   await completeSyncLog(sb, logId, result)
  327:   logger.info('syncProducts complete', { locationId, ...result })
  328:   return result
  329: }

  338: async function buildProductFkCache(sb: ReturnType<typeof Object>, orgId: string): Promise<FkCache> {
  339:   const cache: FkCache = { brands: new Map(), vendors: new Map(), strains: new Map(), categories: new Map() }
  340: 
  341:   const [brands, vendors, strains, categories] = await Promise.all([
  342:     (sb as any).from('brands').select('id, name, external_id').eq('organization_id', orgId).limit(10000),
  343:     (sb as any).from('vendors').select('id, name, external_id').eq('organization_id', orgId).limit(10000),
  344:     (sb as any).from('strains').select('id, name, external_id').eq('organization_id', orgId).limit(10000),
  345:     (sb as any).from('product_categories').select('id, name, external_id').eq('organization_id', orgId).limit(10000),
  346:   ])
  347: 
  348:   for (const b of brands.data ?? []) {
  349:     cache.brands.set(b.name?.toLowerCase(), b.id)
  350:     if (b.external_id) cache.brands.set(`ext:${b.external_id}`, b.id)
  351:   }
  352:   for (const v of vendors.data ?? []) {
  353:     cache.vendors.set(v.name?.toLowerCase(), v.id)
  354:     if (v.external_id) cache.vendors.set(`ext:${v.external_id}`, v.id)
  355:   }
  356:   for (const s of strains.data ?? []) {
  357:     cache.strains.set(s.name?.toLowerCase(), s.id)
  358:     if (s.external_id) cache.strains.set(`ext:${s.external_id}`, s.id)
  359:   }
  360:   for (const c of categories.data ?? []) {

  563: async function upsertLocationPrices(
  564:   sb: ReturnType<typeof Object>,
  565:   orgId: string,
  566:   locationId: string,
  567:   priceRows: Array<{ dutchie_product_id: number; row: Record<string, unknown> }>,
  568:   result: SyncResult,
  569: ): Promise<void> {
  570:   // Reuse the paginated product map instead of a massive .in() query
  571:   const productMap = await buildDutchieProductMap(sb, orgId)
  572: 
  573:   const rows: Record<string, unknown>[] = []
  574:   for (const pr of priceRows) {
  575:     const productId = productMap.get(pr.dutchie_product_id)
  576:     if (!productId) {
  577:       result.skipped++
  578:       continue
  579:     }
  580:     rows.push({ ...pr.row, product_id: productId, location_id: locationId })
  581:   }
  582: 
  583:   await batchUpsert(sb, 'location_product_prices', rows, 'product_id,location_id', result)
  584: }
